 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"You need to find some way to hand it over," said Phia. "I doubt it'll get them off you completely, but if it gets you put just a little lower on their list of priorities it'll be worth it."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Better to keep it," said Jask. "A bargaining chip if they do manage to catch her again."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera hit him.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"They're not going to catch me again. Besides, the justicar already told me that it'd only get me sent to a labor camp instead of the gallows. Screw that. I was talking to Jask, Phia. Telling him that we ought to leave Yorshir and set up in Sahndusk."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Sahndusk, huh? That's not a bad idea. I've never been there, but I know some people who have. It's not much different from here; same kind of city, same kinds of people. Learning the who's who might me tricky, but if you can snatch a purse here you can do it there."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Then we're doing it. Come on, Jask, what's your better idea?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;She knew she could get him to come along. She had to. She talked like it would be nothing, but it did scare her a little. She would need someone watching her back; together they'd be in much better shape than she would be alone.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"I don't know," he said, "You never like my ideas anyway."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Then we're going. We can leave tonight, while it's dark enough to sneak over the city wall."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"We're better off taking some horses," said Phia. "It's a three day ride. I'll go talk to a friend of mine. She knows a lot about Sahndusk, and I can get some advice from her. Grab anything you need for the trip, but stay away from your apartment, Valera. I don't know if they've found it, but it's too much to risk. There's a stables near the south gate we can steal some horses from. I'll take them out the south gate by myself while you two go over the wall, and we'll meet on the road. We can ride from there; if we get out soon, we'll be farther ahead than any news about us."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"You're coming too?" asked Valera. 
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Of course I am. I risked a lot getting you out of that prison. I'm not going to let that go to waste sending you two off on your own to a strange city. I'll come down and help you get started. I can spare a few weeks away from Yorshir."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera smiled. She reached for Phia's hand and pulled her close so that she could hug her without getting up. The sun would set before much longer, but until them it was safer to stay put. Maybe she could even get an hour or so of sleep. 
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Should we let Coddis know?" said Jask. "It'd be crappy to leave him looking for us when we're gone."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No," said Phia, "Make as clean a break as you can. Maybe if things have cooled off one day I'll tell him, but even then... no. Smart thing is for nobody else to know."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera's stomach growled.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Shit, I haven't eaten today at all. I guess my gut's finally unknoted itself. You got any food around here, Jask?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Yeah," he said. "I guess we better go ahead an eat it. It sounds like this will be our last night in Yorshir."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;A minute later Valera was sinking her teeth into some biscuits that probably should have been eaten a few days ago.&nbsp; She didn't worry about it much. She had a lot of planning to do. Her life had changed more than she ever thought it would, and it was time to make something of her own choosing out of it.

Chapter 5


 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Korsk's information was already proving true. He didn't need to wait after he arrived at the house where this 'Phia' woman lived. A woman was inside, and from the sound of it she was busy. He considered breaking in, rushing her, and taking her to question as he had the last one. He didn't even have to use his tools on that one to make her talk.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;He backed off instead, waiting outside in his less conspicuous clothing. Phia was, supposedly, much closer to Valera. Close enough to give him some real resistance. She'd talk, that was a given, but he'd lose valuable time. He would risk following her instead. She wasn't just settling in for the night, not with the hurried footsteps he'd picked up from the other side of her door.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Night had come, the darkness offering to aid his stealthy pursuit. As predicted, her lamps were extinguished and she emerged from the residence, a traveling bag hanging from her shoulder. She was a wary creature, looking behind her and taking an obviously more complicated route than necessary. Her eyes were not practiced enough for seeking shadows, however, and Korsk evaded her attention.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;She stopped at another apartment, one that was too nice to be his target's. He let her knock on the door and gain her entrance before getting close. He lurked in the side alley, outside an open window. He'd missed the first part of the conversation, but he was well in time for what he needed.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Sahndusk. The woman Phia was visiting was telling her how to get to Sahndusk. He listened, making note of each detail. He recognized each landmark mentioned, knowing the route well himself. Phia didn't let the conversation be dragged on after that. She was in a hurry, and Korsk had no doubt that she meant to leave tonight.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;She wouldn't flee to another city just when her friend was in trouble. If he was confident in his information, at least, which he had good reason to be. Valera was either coming with her or already in Sahndusk, needing Phia's help. He could continue following Phia directly, but the longer he did that the more he risked being seen. Besides, if she was going to Sahndusk, he'd be best off fetching his horse. He could be ready to leave in very little time, and if he missed her at the southern gate he'd catch her on the road.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;His course was set. He caught one really good look at her as she left her friend's house. Perhaps he'd get a chance to question her later. He shouldn't have left his special gag in the other girl's mouth.

 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dannis didn't yawn. He sensed it coming, and killed it with raw willpower. He wasn't going to give up his chase so easily, even if he was getting delirious from lack of sleep. He swayed in his saddle, his horse being a necessary replacement for his own legs to keep him going.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;The rest of his gang had scattered long ago, spread out to cast a wider net when their leads ran dry. Dannis doubted that most of them were still looking. Only Geard was still with him.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Now what?" he asked, obviously tired himself.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"We're near the south gate," said Dannis. "We'll ask there to see if anyone's seen him leaving town."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Geard grunted in approval, and after a couple of minutes of the hypnotic clip clop of his horse's shoes they rounded a corner to see the gate down the street. Dannis saw something else interesting enough to cut through his fatigue. It was- what was his name? Did he ever give it? The supposed representative of the jewel crafters stood, holding the reigns of a horse in his hand, talking to one of the guards at the gate.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dannis' old suspicions about him came forth. He put his horse to a trot, but by the time he reached the gate the man was gone, riding into the darkness. He stopped his horse by the guard, hearing Geard slowly catch up to him.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"What were you talking to that man about?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Why is it your business, Master?" he said, sounding suspicious himself.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Because he may have pulled a fraud on me."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"What sort of fraud?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dannis thought of a good lie, before realizing that the truth probably gave him a better case.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"A piece of property was stolen from my sister. I'm searching for it, but I think he may be trying to find it first. Actually, I know he is, he told me. But I'm not sure he intends to give it back if he does."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"I suppose that's fair enough. He asked me if some people passed through tonight. Two men and a woman."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Were a young woman with black hair and a young man with brown curly hair two of them?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"That's them. Wait, are those the thieves?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Yes, they are. Do you have any idea where they were going?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"He didn't say, but Sahndusk is the only real place south of here within five days' ride. I imagine they'll be going through there, at least. If this is about a theft, Master, I'd be negligent of my duty not to tell a justicar."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Sahndusk? That made sense. It was close and they could sell the jewels there. That Justicar Dommia probably wouldn't follow them there, either.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Go tell my father," he said, turning to Geard, "Ask him to send a man to Sahndusk with some things for my stay."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Wait, are you-"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"And then go find a Justicar Dommia, to make our friend here happy."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dannis didn't wait for comment from either man. He struck his horse into a gallop and threw himself into the night, letting only the limited reach of his lantern check his speed. It didn't take him long to overtake the other man, and he shot past him without worry. The dim light would hide his face well enough. He rode ahead, hoping to catch the thief before she got to far. He was well into his journey before wondering- did the guard actually tell him whether the three people had come through or not? 
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera watched the poor girl struggling on her bed. Hogtied, blindfolded, and gagged in her underclothes with strips of own gown. She was such a pretty, delicate thing, begging in a pathetic whimper.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;She raised her weapon, a short, thin whip. She let it fall. The girl screamed, muffled by the gag, and a red line appeared on her thigh. Valera rolled her onto the side, an odd position for her with her legs still spread. She could watch every gentle motion of the bound girl's body, every small muscle tense and relax, every heave of her chest, and every subtle shift of her frame as she tried to find some mercy in how she was tied. She could see every way that her bindings held her in a shape that caused her such anguish and terror. She could see how she begged not just with her whimpering, but with her entire body as her bound limbs pulled against knots that she knew wouldn't give.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera painted her body red. Her victim's screams and thrashing took on every character imaginable. It didn't matter. Valera held all of the power, and it was her desire to see this girl suffer.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;As her arm swung the whip, over and over, she became aware of someone standing behind her, guiding her hand and showing her how to put the most cruelty possible into every lash. Valera accepted it. It was the justicar, teaching her craft. Valera let herself learn. Only when she heard the laugh over her shoulder did Valera notice her red skin, her talon-like nails, and her unnaturally hot breath flowing onto her neck. She felt something on her leg, and looked down to see a tail wrapping around it.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"It's your turn."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera saw the girl, now untied and holding the strips of cloth in her hand. She didn't resist. Luccela held her arms while the girl stripped her. She held her down on the bed while she was tied up, twice as tight as the girl had been. She opened her mouth willingly to allow it to be stuffed with a gag still soaked in the other girl's saliva.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;She saw Luccela stand behind the girl, but the whip in her hand, and show her how to raise it. Valera closed her eyes. The next moment was as painful as she expected.

 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia heard a knock on her office door. It took her a bit of time to understand this, since she'd heard it while sleeping. By the view from her window showed it was early morning. 
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Come," she said, sitting and wiping the sleep from her eyes. 
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Back to work, it was. She was Justicar Dommia Bethor. Losing a prisoner was inexcusable, and she'd put it right if she had to die doing it. The few hours of sleep she'd allowed herself were a necessity, not a luxury. Her line of work required a clear head, after all. And now she had one again. So back to work.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;A young man, about her age, entered. He had foppish blond hair and a measure of charm to his face. She didn't recognize him, but his clothing gave away his class.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Hello, Mistress," said the man. "I, uh, have some information about a criminal you're hunting for."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia was too good a detective not to notice that he was trying to get a better look at her body, particularly her ass, hidden from his side of the desk.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Which one?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"The one that attacked poor Bescie. There wouldn't happen to be some kind of reward, would there?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"If what you say turns out to be useful, yes, there's a small sum to be had."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Well," he said, sitting on her desk, "I have something worth more than a small sum. Maybe you can offer an alternative? Some other way to make it worth my time? You know, you look like you've been working awfully hard-"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia did not have time for this. She wished that she did; if it was Sir Elchar here...
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"That was clumsy and awful. Get off my desk and tell me what you know before I have you flogged."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;He took her seriously.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"I was with Dannis, Bescie's brother, last night. We had been hunting for the thief ourselves, and we finally found something when he questioned one of the guards at the south gate. Turns out they're skipping town. They're going to Sahndusk."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Wait, who is 'they'? And if you found out about this last night, why are you only telling me now?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Oh, the thief has a guy name Jask with her. There's another woman, too; I don't know what she's doing with them. When Dannis took off after them he told me to go tell his father, and I was pretty tired, and figured I'd spend the night. His sister is still having a difficult time, you know."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"So your friend rode off alone after three potentially dangerous criminals, and you spent the night trying to seduce his traumatized sister instead of coming to tell me right away?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;The man's face was turning red.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"That's not fair at all. If anything ever did happen between me and Bescie- which it hasn't- it would be because-"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Stop. I want the whole story, starting from the morning after the robbery, right now."

 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera groaned, rolling over to resist Jask's prodding. He was trying to wake her up, the bastard.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Come on, it's way past sunrise. We need to get going."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Why? nobody's waiting on us," she said, burying her face in her arms.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"What if somebody is following us? We'll be easy to find on the road."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Then we should stay here."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Trying to travel last night hadn't gone well. Riding a horse was more difficult than Valera expected, especially at night when they couldn't see. She and Jask were hopeless, and before they got too far they had to dismount and find a campsite. What they settled on was a clear spot on the other side of a patch of forest. It hid them from the road, but other than that all it offered was some grass to sleep on.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;None of them had any camping gear. They were in a hurry to leave the city, particularly hoping to get out before the stables noticed three missing horses. Valera had almost nothing with her save for the money from her stash, most of it from selling the jewelry. They had a single lantern between them and some food and water. All three of them wound up sleeping on bare ground.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Well, if you're not going anywhere, I might as well tie you up."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Jask started to make good on his word, and she felt him climb over and straddle her body.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Hey!"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera scrambled out from under him and got to her feet.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"You prick," she said, brushing grass off her clothes.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"At least I'm a clever prick."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Where's Phia?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Peeing, I think."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Valera checked her pocket. It was still there.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"What's that?" he asked.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Huh, oh," she said, looking around to make sure they were alone. She pulled the necklace out just enough to show him.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Lookit."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"That's- You told Phia that you wrapped that up and gave it a soldier as something for that justicar!"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Quiet! After all I've been through over this thing? Tied up, chained up, beat up, whipped, nearly killed- I'm going to get paid for this, even if it turns out to be fake and only worth a cold lunch."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"You got whipped?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Yeah," she said, solemnly, "and even-"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;No, Jask didn't need to hear about the kiss. Valera just wished she had a chance to pay her back. She put the necklace away.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Nevermind. I'm going to sell this damn thing. I have to now. Don't tell Phia."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Jask shook his head, but Valera knew he'd keep quiet. He was no snitch, and he was in this with her now. A little something more to get started with in Sahndusk wouldn't hurt, and he knew it.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Finally, you're up."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Phia came out of the trees, looking far too groomed for their circumstances.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"How close is the first inn?" asked Valera.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Maybe we should avoid those," said Jask. "That's the first place anyone following us will stop to look. Or ask about."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"We'll find a farmer's house next time," said Phia. "We'll tell him the inn was full. We might have to sleep in a barn, but at least they'll be a roof and some straw to sleep on. We can probably buy food from him too.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;They mounted their horses, and as the sun rose higher in the sky Valera started to get a handle on managing the beast. Soon she was comfortable enough to start paying attention to the land around her. She'd never been in such a wide open space, not a building in sight, and it somehow seemed peaceful, despite making her nervous. The smell was unfamiliar- the air was just missing something. The quiet was strange.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;The didn't talk much- traveling mostly in silence. Valera started remembering her dream. It was nothing like the one with the demoness. It wasn't nearly as lucid or real. But she didn't want to think she'd dream like that of her own accord. The sooner she could get rid of the necklace the better.

 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia's horse was sluggish, too tired to keep the pace she wanted. Three soldiers lagged even farther behind, now six hours into their ride. Dommia hoped they'd hold out. Ahead of then was the inn, the first most likely stop for any one of the people she was after, and she didn't want to rest until she arrived there. That way she could at least do some questioning while they waited for the horses to recover. If she was luck, a fresh horse might be had.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Her real hope had been to find the thief and her confederates by now. They had a head start on her, but if they were on foot she still might catch up to them at any moment. The open farmland gave her a good view,&nbsp; but not a perfect one. She'd asked for reports of stolen horses, but didn't have time to wait for an answer.
She and her bear endured the road for a while longer before they saw a building on the side of the road, revealed to them after coming over the crest of a hill. She rallied her mount and her followers and finished this first leg of their hunt. 
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Domain's feet hit dirt. She took her horse by the reigns and lead her over to the stables, or what passed for them. It was little more than a cover jutting out from the main&nbsp; building, not where she'd want to leave her over a cold winter night. There was only a single horse currently there. Dommia might be able to make a deal with its owner.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Her soldiers followed her inside, finding a cozy commons inside with a handful of travelers and an old man putting a meal of bread and cheese in front of them.&nbsp; She scanned each of their faces, not finding any that were of interest to her. It didn't take them long to notice her and show a nervous concern.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"My name is Justicar Dommia Bethor, and I am in currently I pursuit of a known thief, a suspicious individual, and an impetuous imbecile. All coming from the north, arriving last night or this morning. Is this everyone on the premises right here?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, Mistress," said the old man. She knew well the look of a many who just didn't want trouble, and was inclined to believe him.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"There's a man upstairs. He arrived just before morning, barely talking sense. He asked about three people he was looking for, but I haven't seen anyone like that. He took a bed and hasn't woken up yet."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Barely talking sense. That sounded like Dannis.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Was there another man? He would be easy to spot; he was very tall and we'll dressed."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Yes- he came by as well, a few hours ago. He didn't stay for long, just to eat."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Have you seen anything else relevant or suspicious?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, Mistress. It's been nicely quiet."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Thank you for your assistance," she said before addressing her soldiers, "Let's go wake up our friend."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia found the stairs and climbed them. There was only one door shut, which she promptly beat her fist against.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Master Culthorip, this is Justicar Dommia-"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Shit!"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"-Bethor. Open up right now."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"The damn morning's gone!"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Now, while I'm still in only a bad mood."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Not today!"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia heard a window open and his voice trail off. She immediately broke into action, pushing between her own shocked men and bounding down the stairs. She leaped over a table to reach the exit with her best haste, but even as she slammed the door out of her way, grabbing the frame to swing her momentum toward the horses, she was too late. Dannis's mount was out of the stables and he was hoisting himself into the saddle while on the move. He stopped once in control and out of Dommia's reach.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"I won't settle for a bad mood, so perhaps I'll see you in Sahndusk. With your job done for you, I hope."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Master Culthorip, I will have you arrest and flogged right along with Valera and her cohorts."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Is that her name? I don't think I knew that yet. Good woman! Pay the innkeeper for me!"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dannis wheeled his horse and took off.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Are we going to follow him?" asked a soldier, catching up to her.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, his horse is rested and ours aren't. Besides, he's not the important one. We'll find him when we find the thief."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia had never punished a man the way she did her female playthings, but this one was giving her the urge, and she'd make sure he didn't enjoy it.

 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Phia woke from her sleep. She rose from her makeshift bed in the cellar they'd snuck into for the night. The place felt oddly suffocating now, and she desperately wanted to get out into the open air. She padded over to the cellar doors, a hatch that opened to the outside with a roughly built set of stairs to lead up to it.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;When she reached it she pushed, but it stayed put. There wasn't a latch on the outside, and the bar on the inside was gone. She tried again, but it was stuck. She started banging on it, only dimly aware that she should be keeping quiet.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"What are you doing?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Phia jumped, only to see it was Valera standing at her side.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"I need to get out."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Oh," she said, oddly distant, "You'll need my help to do that."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"What? It should just open! I can't see anything stopping it."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Of course it won't open," said Jask, frightening her again with his sudden appearance. "It's supposed to hold you in. It's a prison after all."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, that's not right," said Phia, trying to remember how they got into the cellar in the first place.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"We can help her," said Valera, slowly wrapping her hands around Phia's arm.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Jask took her other arm, and before Phia could ask them to stop they pushed her down to her knees.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Let go," she said, pleading, but they ignored her. Jask twisted her arm to keep her still while Valera locked a heavy iron collar around her neck. A thick chain hanging from the back dangled behind her, and she heard it rattle as Jask and Valera worked together to put shackles on her wrists.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Valera... why..."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Chains started weaving around her torso and arms, coiling around and crossing in an intricate pattern. She heard locks being fastened behind her back, and every time one did the chains grew tighter and tighter, crushing the breath out of her.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Jask lifted her to her feet while Valera put them in irons as well. She had trouble keeping upright, not being able to stand straight because of the shortness of the chains that ran from her collar to her ankles. Jask and Valera took places on her flanks and guided her deeper into the cellar, down hallways and into a room that light simply couldn't stand to be in.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Phia could see almost nothing, but when her escorts threw her to her knees again she could make out the cage in front of her.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, you wouldn't do this. Valera! Why?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"She wants us to."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;She tried to resist them, but they slowly and calmly forced her into the cage, folding her body so that she was kneeling with her torso bend over her legs, balled up to just be squeezed into the tiny cell. They sealed it shut, and then simply stood and walked away.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Come back!" she called, her voice weakening as she continued, "Don't leave me her..."

It didn't surprise him too much; Mistress Dommia was precisely the kind of woman who would ride straight to the keep upon entering the city gates to receive his report. The woman's commitment to duty was absolute.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Justicar," he said. "Welcome back. Things have been in order; you won't find much that needs your attention, at least not right away. Did you catch the fugitives?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Dommia removed her helmet and sat down on her desk. He'd never seen her do that before. She was strangely relaxed, especially given that she must be coming in from at least three days of riding. More, if she'd been hauling prisoners.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Yes, all three. Well, I should say two. One of them didn't survive to see a dungeon."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Captain Bunt was taken aback by her casual attitude toward the affair.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"Are the prisoners here now?"
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, we didn't bother bringing them back. We let Count Dhern hang the both of them. Saved us the hassle. Master Dannis made off with his sister's necklace. The whole thing is pretty much wrapped up now."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Captain Bunt couldn't find fault on any particular point. Letting the thieves be hanged in Sahndusk was certainly reasonable. But the Dommia Bethor he knew would never let "the hassle" stop her from hanging them from her own gallows to make sure that everyone in the city knew that justice had been served.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;He left her chair to stand in front of her desk, expecting her to take her seat. She stayed where she was, toying with helmet.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"So, is there anything exciting I should know about? Any prisoners to interrogate? I would love a good interrogation about now."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"No, Mistress. I suppose there is one small matter, if you wouldn't rather rest from your journey first, but it's hardly urgent. Lord Hennisfair wanted to know if you could stop by to discuss something when you returned. He wasn't specific about what, but he said it was a matter you were familiar with."
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;The justicar looked up at him and smiled. He'd never seen that kind of smile on her face before, and it made the hair stand up on the back of his neck.
 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;"I know what he needs help with," she said. "I'll be very, very happy to serve."
